> no honey i already ran the first script with both teh court binders and war room and i already made the  templates too, i just need to do the map and copy over from legacy folder.

### Assistant
> Got it. Then you do **not** need the full builder again. You need a **single-purpose migration script** that:
> 
> - Uses your existing `FCFCU_CASE` structure
> - Copies from `__legacy` into your **already-created** War Room/Court folders per your mapping
> - Applies **prefix-only** rename (`PREFIX__OriginalName`)
> - Writes to a **migration log** (and creates it if missing)
> 
> Below is exactly that.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Legacy → New (COPY + PREFIX + LOG) — Migration-Only PowerShell
> 
> **What it does**
> - Copies files from legacy subfolders to your target folders
> - Prefixes filenames
> - Creates `MIGRATION_LOG.csv` and `MIGRATION_NOTES.md` if missing
> - Optional SHA256 hashing (defaults ON; turn OFF if you have huge media)
> 
> ```powershell
> # ==========================================
> # FCFCU Legacy Migration ONLY (COPY + PREFIX + LOG)
> # ==========================================
> param(
>   [string]$legacyPath = ".\__legacy",
>   [string]$caseRoot   = ".\FCFCU_CASE",
>   [bool]$hash = $true
> )
> 
> function Ensure-Dir($p){ New-Item -ItemType Directory -Force -Path $p | Out-Null }
> function Ensure-File($p, $content){
>   Ensure-Dir (Split-Path $p -Parent)
>   Set-Content -Path $p -Value $content -Encoding UTF8
> }
> function Append-Content($p, $content){
>   Ensure-Dir (Split-Path $p -Parent)
>   Add-Content -Path $p -Value $content -Encoding UTF8
> }
> function NowIso(){ (Get-Date).ToString("yyyy-MM-ddTHH:mm:ss") }
> function Sha256($p){
>   if (-not $hash) { return "" }
>   try { return (Get-FileHash -Algorithm SHA256 -Path $p).Hash } catch { return "" }
> }
> 
> if (-not (Test-Path $legacyPath)) { throw "legacyPath not found: $legacyPath" }
> Ensure-Dir $caseRoot
> 
> $warRoot   = Join-Path $caseRoot "02_WAR_ROOM"
> $courtRoot = Join-Path $caseRoot "01_COURT_BINDER\FCFCU-49D03-2501-MF-002559"
> $archRoot  = Join-Path $caseRoot "99_ARCHIVE"
> Ensure-Dir $warRoot
> Ensure-Dir $courtRoot
> Ensure-Dir $archRoot
> 
> # ---- Logs (create if missing)
> $logCsv = Join-Path $caseRoot "MIGRATION_LOG.csv"
> $logMd  = Join-Path $caseRoot "MIGRATION_NOTES.md"
> 
> if (-not (Test-Path $logCsv)) {
>   Ensure-File $logCsv "timestamp,action,src,dst,old_name,new_name,sha256,rule"
> }
> if (-not (Test-Path $logMd)) {
>   Ensure-File $logMd @"
> # Migration Notes
> Created: $(NowIso)
> 
> Mode: COPY
> Rename policy: PREFIX + '__' + OriginalName
> Purpose: Move legacy content into the new binder/war-room structure while preserving __legacy intact.
> 
> "@
> }
> 
> function LogRow($action,$src,$dst,$old,$new,$h,$rule){
>   $line = "{0},{1},""{2}"",""{3}"",""{4}"",""{5}"",{6},""{7}""" -f (NowIso),$action,$src,$dst,$old,$new,$h,$rule
>   Append-Content $logCsv $line
> }
> 
> function CopyWithLog($src,$dst,$rule){
>   Ensure-Dir (Split-Path $dst -Parent)
>   Copy-Item -LiteralPath $src -Destination $dst -Force
>   $old = Split-Path $src -Leaf
>   $new = Split-Path $dst -Leaf
>   $h = Sha256 $dst
>   LogRow "COPY" $src $dst $old $new $h $rule
> }
> 
> # ==========================================
> # MAPPING TABLE (EDIT HERE if needed)
> # NOTE: dest is RELATIVE to War Room unless rule says otherwise.
> # ==========================================
> $map = @(
>   # ADMIN / TRACKERS / TIMELINE / OVERVIEWS
>   @{ src="00_admin\00_trackers"; destRoot="WAR"; dest="WI_INTERNAL_REFERENCE\WI8_02_DAMAGES_AND_SETTLEMENT"; prefix="WI8.02.010"; rule="ADMIN_TRACKERS_TO_WI8.02" },
>   @{ src="00_admin\05_timeline";  destRoot="WAR"; dest="WA_ANCHOR_OVERVIEW\WA0_00_COMMAND_MAP";          prefix="WA0.00.030"; rule="TIMELINE_TO_WA0.00" },
>   @{ src="00_admin\10_overviews"; destRoot="WAR"; dest="WE_EFFECTS_PROCEDURAL_CHAIN\WE4_00_CHAIN_ANALYSIS"; prefix="WE4.00.010"; rule="OVERVIEWS_TO_WE4.00" },
> 
>   # STRATEGY

>   @{ src="00_admin\20_strategy\20_jurisdiction_service_tr_4_1_b"; destRoot="WAR"; dest="WB_BASIS_ISSUE_AND_LAW\WB1_00_LAW_RESEARCH"; prefix="WB1.00.010"; rule="SERVICE_LAW_TO_WB1.00" },

> 
>   # DRAFTS / TEMPLATES
>   @{ src="00_admin\30_drafts-templates\10_motions"; destRoot="WAR"; dest="WC_CLAIMS_AND_MOTIONS\WC2_00_DRAFT_MOTIONS"; prefix="WC2.00.010"; rule="MOTION_DRAFTS_TO_WC2.00" },
>   @{ src="00_admin\30_drafts-templates\20_declarations_affidavits"; destRoot="WAR"; dest="WF_FACTS_DECLARATIONS\WF5_01_DRAFT_DECLARATIONS"; prefix="WF5.01.010"; rule="DECL_DRAFTS_TO_WF5.01" },

> 
>   # FILINGS (stage into War Room intake; you will PROMOTE selectively later)

>

>   @{ src="personal_narrative\04_Donations_and_Support"; destRoot="WAR"; dest="WI_INTERNAL_REFERENCE\WI8_01_PUBLIC_ADVOCACY"; prefix="WI8.01.050"; rule="DONATIONS_TO_WI8.01" },
>   @{ src="personal_narrative\05_Timeline"; destRoot="WAR"; dest="WA_ANCHOR_OVERVIEW\WA0_00_COMMAND_MAP"; prefix="WA0.00.060"; rule="NARR_TIMELINE_TO_WA0.00" },
> 
>   # TOOLS -> ARCHIVE (keep separate)
>   @{ src="tools"; destRoot="ARCH"; dest="tools_legacy"; prefix="ARCH.010"; rule="TOOLS_TO_ARCHIVE" }
> )
> 
> # ---- Ensure special internal folder exists (if you didn't already create it)
> Ensure-Dir (Join-Path $warRoot "WI_INTERNAL_REFERENCE\WI8_99_INTERNAL_ONLY")
> 
> # ---- Run migration
> foreach ($m in $map) {
>   $srcRoot = Join-Path $legacyPath $m.src
>   if (-not (Test-Path $srcRoot)) { continue }
> 
>   $dstBase =
>     if ($m.destRoot -eq "ARCH") { Join-Path $archRoot $m.dest }
>     elseif ($m.destRoot -eq "COURT") { Join-Path $courtRoot $m.dest }
>     else { Join-Path $warRoot $m.dest }
> 
>   Ensure-Dir $dstBase
> 
>   Get-ChildItem -LiteralPath $srcRoot -Recurse -File | ForEach-Object {
>     $rel = $_.FullName.Substring($srcRoot.Length).TrimStart('\','/')
>     $destDir = Join-Path $dstBase (Split-Path $rel -Parent)
> 
>     $oldName = $_.Name
>     $newName = "{0}__{1}" -f $m.prefix, $oldName
>     $destPath = Join-Path $destDir $newName
> 
>     CopyWithLog $_.FullName $destPath $m.rule
>   }
> }
> 
> Write-Host "DONE: Legacy migrated into existing structure (COPY)."
> Write-Host "Log: $logCsv"
> Write-Host "Notes: $logMd"
> Write-Host "Hashing: $hash"
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## How to run it (minimal)
> From the folder that contains both `__legacy` and `FCFCU_CASE`:
> 
> ```powershell
> .\migrate_legacy_only.ps1 -legacyPath ".\__legacy" -caseRoot ".\FCFCU_CASE" -hash $false
> ```
> 
> Use `-hash $false` if you have lots of videos; turn it on later for PDFs/exhibits.
>

> ## One fast correctness check (so you don’t waste time)
> After it runs, confirm:
> - `FCFCU_CASE\MIGRATION_LOG.csv` exists and has **more than 1 line**
> - You see files under:
>   - `FCFCU_CASE\02_WAR_ROOM\WZ_PROMOTION_PIPELINE\WZ9_00_050_FILINGS_INTAKE\`
>   - `FCFCU_CASE\02_WAR_ROOM\WI_INTERNAL_REFERENCE\WI8_00_DOCKET_RECORD\`
> 
> If either is empty, it means your legacy path differs (common when legacy is nested deeper).
>

### Assistant
> Got it. Your tree is solid. What’s missing is **a deterministic linking spine** so Obsidian has *zero excuse* to leave notes floating.
> 
> Here’s the rule that makes this dummy-proof:
> 
> ## The No-Orphans Rule (Simple)
> Every note must be reachable from **at least one** of these:
> 
> 1) `FCFCU_CASE/README.md` (Vault Root Map)  
> 2) `01_COURT_BINDER/.../A0.00.010_MASTER_CASE_INDEX.md` (Court Binder Master Index)  
> 3) `02_WAR_ROOM/.../WA0.00.000_WAR_ROOM_OVERVIEW.md` (War Room Master Index)  
> 4) Its own folder `_README.md` (Folder Index)
> 
> If a file doesn’t have a parent link from one of those, it will drift in graph space.
> 
> Below are **ready-to-copy** contents for the key index files + a repeatable section cover pattern that links everything.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 1) VAULT ROOT MAP
> Create/overwrite:
> 
> `FCFCU_CASE/README.md`
> 
> ```markdown
> ---
> title: FCFCU Case Vault Root
> case_id: 49D03-2501-MF-002559
> type: vault_root
> ---
> 
> # FCFCU Case Vault Root (49D03-2501-MF-002559)
> 
> ## Primary Workstreams
> - [[01_COURT_BINDER/FCFCU-49D03-2501-MF-002559/A_ANCHOR_OVERVIEW/A0_00_COVER_INDEX/A0.00.010_MASTER_CASE_INDEX|Court Binder — Master Index]]
> - [[02_WAR_ROOM/WA_ANCHOR_OVERVIEW/WA0_00_COMMAND_MAP/WA0.00.000_WAR_ROOM_OVERVIEW|War Room — Command Map]]
> 
> ## Templates
> - [[03_OBSIDIAN_TEMPLATES/TEMPLATE_SECTION_COVER|TEMPLATE_SECTION_COVER]]
> - [[03_OBSIDIAN_TEMPLATES/TEMPLATE_SECTION_INDEX|TEMPLATE_SECTION_INDEX]]
> - [[03_OBSIDIAN_TEMPLATES/TEMPLATE_COURT_DOC|TEMPLATE_COURT_DOC]]
> - [[03_OBSIDIAN_TEMPLATES/TEMPLATE_WAR_NOTE|TEMPLATE_WAR_NOTE]]
> 
> ## Archive / Migration
> - [[99_ARCHIVE/MIGRATION_NOTES|MIGRATION_NOTES]]
> - [[99_ARCHIVE/MIGRATION_LOG|MIGRATION_LOG]]
> - [[99_ARCHIVE/PROMOTION_CHECKLIST|PROMOTION_CHECKLIST]]
> 
> ## Navigation Notes
> - Court Binder is designed for printing. War Room is designed for strategy, drafting, and intake.
> - Anything “internal only” belongs in War Room (or Court Binder Tab I).
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # 2) COURT BINDER MASTER INDEX (SPINE)
> Your file exists:
> 
> `01_COURT_BINDER/FCFCU-49D03-2501-MF-002559/A_ANCHOR_OVERVIEW/A0_00_COVER_INDEX/A0.00.010_MASTER_CASE_INDEX.md`
> 
> Replace contents with:
> 
> ```markdown
> ---
> title: Master Case Index
> case_id: 49D03-2501-MF-002559
> binder: court
> type: master_index
> ---
> 
> # Master Case Index (Court Binder)
> 
> **Case:** FCFCU v. Cody Rice-Velasquez  
> **Cause No.:** 49D03-2501-MF-002559
> 
> ## Tabs (Court Binder)
> - **A — Anchor Overview**
>   - [[../A0.00.000_SECTION_COVER|A0.00.000 Section Cover]]
>   - [[../A0_01_OVERVIEW/A0.01.001_ONE_PAGE_CASE_SUMMARY|A0.01.001 One Page Case Summary]]
>   - [[../A0_01_OVERVIEW/A0.01.002_HEARING_SCOPE_AND_RELIEF|A0.01.002 Hearing Scope & Relief]]
>

### User
> I NEED A SCRIPT TO CHECK AND CORRECT FRONT MATTER AND UPDATE INDEXES PYTHON SCRIPT PLEASE, BUT FIRST WE NEED TO LOCK-IN WHAT FRONT MATTER SHOULD BE THERE.

### Assistant
> You’re right to force this step. If we don’t lock the front matter spec, any “fixer” script will just spray inconsistency faster.
> 
> Below is a **locked-in front matter standard** for your FCFCU vault that is:
> 
> - Minimal (won’t annoy you later)
> - Deterministic (scriptable)
> - Graph-friendly (consistent “type” + “case_id”)
> - Safe across Court Binder vs War Room vs Templates vs Archive
> - Works even without Dataview
> 
> After the spec, I’m giving you the **Python script** that:
> 1) Scans all `.md` files
> 2) Adds/fixes YAML front matter per the rules
> 3) Normalizes keys
> 4) Writes a log + CSV
> 5) Rebuilds/updates folder `_README.md` indexes (optional but included)
> 6) Updates the Court Binder + War Room master indexes (optional section; you can turn it on/off)
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Front Matter Standard (LOCKED)
> 
> ### Global keys (allowed everywhere)
> These keys may appear in any note:
> 
> - `title` (string) — human title
> - `type` (enum string) — required for all case vault notes except pure scratch notes
> - `case_id` (string) — required for all case vault notes in FCFCU case
> - `binder` (enum string) — `court` | `war_room` | `templates` | `archive`
> - `tab` (string) — e.g., `A`, `B`, `C2`, `WA`, `WB1` (only if relevant)
> - `id` (string) — the document code prefix (e.g., `C2.01.001`) if present in filename
> - `created` (YYYY-MM-DD) — optional; script will not invent unless you want it to
> - `updated` (YYYY-MM-DD) — script can set on modification (recommended)
> - `visibility` (enum string) — `public` | `internal_only` (optional)
> - `print` (bool) — for binder printing logic (optional)
> - `tags` (list) — optional, lightweight
> 
> ### `type` enum (approved list)
> Use ONLY these. This is what prevents chaos.
> 
> - `vault_root` — the vault root README (FCFCU_CASE/README.md)
> - `master_index` — the two spine indexes (Court binder + War room)
> - `folder_index` — `_README.md` files that index a folder
> - `section_cover` — `*.000_SECTION_COVER.md`
> - `section_index` — if you create dedicated section index pages (optional)
> - `court_doc` — narrative docs used in filings (motions, declarations, analysis)
> - `evidence_map` — evidence index/log/map docs
> - `template` — anything in `03_OBSIDIAN_TEMPLATES`
> - `admin` — trackers, logs, migration notes
> - `legacy` — anything under legacy mirrors
> - `scratch` — anything you explicitly don’t want structured
> 
> ### Required rules (non-negotiable)
> 1) **Every `.md` inside `01_COURT_BINDER` and `02_WAR_ROOM` MUST have:**
>    - `type`
>    - `case_id`
>    - `binder`
> 
> 2) `case_id` fixed value:
>    - `49D03-2501-MF-002559`
> 
> 3) `binder` derived from path:
>    - `01_COURT_BINDER` → `court`
>    - `02_WAR_ROOM` → `war_room`
>    - `03_OBSIDIAN_TEMPLATES` → `templates`
>    - `99_ARCHIVE` → `archive`
> 
> 4) `title`:
>    - If already present, keep.
>    - Else derive from filename (strip code prefix, replace underscores with spaces).
> 
> 5) `id` and `tab`:
>    - If filename begins with something like `C2.01.001_...` then:
>      - `id: C2.01.001`
>      - `tab: C` (or `C2` if you want; I recommend `C` for binder tabs, `C2` for subtab)
>    - War Room docs like `WA0.01.002_...`:
>      - `tab: WA`
> 
> 6) `updated`:
>    - Script sets `updated: YYYY-MM-DD` when it changes a file.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## The Script (Python) — Front Matter Fix + Index Updates
> 
> ### What it does
> - Walks the folder you run it from (default: current directory)
> - For each `.md` file:
>   - Reads YAML front matter if present
>   - Normalizes keys
>   - Adds missing required keys based on path
>   - Derives `title`, `id`, `tab`
>   - Writes back only if changes are needed
> - Generates:
>   - `FRONTMATTER_FIX_LOG.md`
>   - `FRONTMATTER_FIX_LOG.csv`
> - Builds/updates `_README.md` in each folder that contains `.md` files (optional, on by default)
> 
> ### Copy/paste as: `fix_frontmatter_and_indexes.py`
> 
> ```python
> from __future__ import annotations
> 
> import argparse
> import csv
> import datetime as dt
> import os
> import re
> from dataclasses import dataclass
> from pathlib import Path
> from typing import Dict, List, Optional, Tuple
> 
> # -----------------------------
> # LOCKED FRONT MATTER STANDARD
> # -----------------------------
> CASE_ID = "49D03-2501-MF-002559"
> 
> TYPE_ENUM = {
>     "vault_root",
>     "master_index",
>     "folder_index",
>     "section_cover",
>     "section_index",
>     "court_doc",
>     "evidence_map",
>     "template",
>     "admin",
>     "legacy",
>     "scratch",
> }
> 
> BINDER_BY_PATH = {
>     "01_COURT_BINDER": "court",
>     "02_WAR_ROOM": "war_room",
>     "03_OBSIDIAN_TEMPLATES": "templates",
>     "99_ARCHIVE": "archive",
> }
> 
> # Determines required keys for case vault notes
> REQUIRED_KEYS = ["type", "case_id", "binder"]
> 
> # Files we never auto-touch (add patterns as needed)
> SKIP_FILENAMES = {
>     ".obsidian.md",  # example placeholder
> }
> 
> ID_PREFIX_RE = re.compile(r"^(?P<id>[A-Z]{1,2}\d?(?:\.\d{2})?\.\d{3,4})_", re.IGNORECASE)
> # Examples matched:
> # C2.01.001_..., A0.00.010_..., H7.01.0001_..., WA0.00.000_...
> 
> 
> @dataclass
> class FixResult:
>     path: Path
>     changed: bool
>     reason: str
> 
> 
> def today_ymd() -> str:
>     return dt.date.today().isoformat()
> 
> 
> def detect_binder(path: Path) -> Optional[str]:
>     parts = {p for p in path.parts}
>     for folder, binder in BINDER_BY_PATH.items():
>         if folder in parts:
>             return binder
>     return None
> 
> 
> def derive_id_and_tab(filename: str) -> Tuple[Optional[str], Optional[str]]:
>     m = ID_PREFIX_RE.match(filename)
>     if not m:
>         return None, None
>     doc_id = m.group("id")
>     # tab heuristics: first 1-2 letters at start (WA, WB, etc.) OR single letter for court tabs
>     # For "C2.01.001" -> tab "C"
>     # For "WA0.00.000" -> tab "WA"
>     tab_match = re.match(r"^([A-Z]{1,2})", doc_id, re.IGNORECASE)
>     tab = tab_match.group(1).upper() if tab_match else None
>     # If tab is like "C2" and you prefer "C" as binder tab, reduce to first letter for court binder
>     if tab and len(tab) == 2 and tab[1].isdigit():
>         tab = tab[0]
>     return doc_id, tab
> 
> 
> def title_from_filename(filename: str) -> str:
>     # Strip extension
>     base = filename.rsplit(".", 1)[0]
>     # Remove ID prefix like C2.01.001_
>     base = ID_PREFIX_RE.sub("", base)
>     # Clean
>     base = base.replace("_", " ").strip()
>     # Title case but preserve common legal acronyms
>     # (This is intentionally conservative; doesn't smash case too hard)
>     return base if base else "Untitled"
> 
> 
> def split_frontmatter(text: str) -> Tuple[Optional[str], str]:
>     """
>     Returns (yaml_text_or_none, body_text)
>     """
>     if not text.startswith("---\n"):
>         return None, text
>     # find second '---' line
>     end = text.find("\n---\n", 4)
>     if end == -1:
>         return None, text  # malformed; treat as no front matter
>     yaml_text = text[4:end]  # between the --- lines
>     body = text[end + 5 :]   # after \n---\n
>     return yaml_text, body
> 
> 
> def parse_simple_yaml(yaml_text: str) -> Dict[str, object]:
>     """
>     Minimal YAML parser:
>     - key: value
>     - key: [a, b]
>     - key:
>         - item
>     This avoids external dependencies.
>     """
>     data: Dict[str, object] = {}
>     lines = [ln.rstrip("\n") for ln in yaml_text.splitlines()]
>     i = 0
>     current_key = None
>     list_acc: List[str] = []
>     in_list = False
> 
>     def commit_list():
>         nonlocal current_key, list_acc, in_list
>         if current_key is not None and in_list:
>             data[current_key] = list_acc[:]
>         current_key = None
>         list_acc = []
>         in_list = False
> 
>     while i < len(lines):
>         ln = lines[i].strip()
>         i += 1
>         if not ln or ln.startswith("#"):
>             continue
> 
>         # list item
>         if ln.startswith("- "):
>             if current_key is None:
>                 continue
>             in_list = True
>             list_acc.append(ln[2:].strip())
>             continue
> 
>         # key: value
>         if ":" in ln:
>             commit_list()
>             key, val = ln.split(":", 1)
>             key = key.strip()
>             val = val.strip()
> 
>             if val == "":
>                 # Could be multiline list
>                 current_key = key
>                 in_list = False
>                 list_acc = []
>                 continue
> 
>             # inline list [a, b]
>             if val.startswith("[") and val.endswith("]"):
>                 inner = val[1:-1].strip()
>                 items = [x.strip() for x in inner.split(",") if x.strip()]
>                 data[key] = items
>                 continue
> 
>             # bool
>             if val.lower() in ("true", "false"):
>                 data[key] = (val.lower() == "true")
>                 continue
> 
>             # string (strip quotes if present)
>             if (val.startswith('"') and val.endswith('"')) or (val.startswith("'") and val.endswith("'")):
>                 val = val[1:-1]
>             data[key] = val
>             continue
> 
>     commit_list()
>     return data
> 
> 
> def dump_simple_yaml(data: Dict[str, object]) -> str:
>     """
>     Deterministic YAML emitter:
>     - sorted keys (but keep a preferred order first)
>     """
>     preferred_order = [
>         "title",
>         "type",
>         "case_id",
>         "binder",
>         "tab",
>         "id",
>         "visibility",
>         "print",
>         "created",
>         "updated",
>         "tags",
>     ]
>     keys = []
>     for k in preferred_order:
>         if k in data:
>             keys.append(k)
>     for k in sorted(data.keys()):
>         if k not in keys:
>             keys.append(k)
> 
>     out_lines: List[str] = []
>     for k in keys:
>         v = data[k]
>         if isinstance(v, list):
>             out_lines.append(f"{k}:")
>             for item in v:
>                 out_lines.append(f"  - {item}")
>         elif isinstance(v, bool):
>             out_lines.append(f"{k}: {'true' if v else 'false'}")
>         else:
>             # quote only if needed
>             s = str(v)
>             if any(ch in s for ch in [":", "#", "[", "]", "{", "}", "\n"]):
>                 s = s.replace('"', '\\"')
>                 out_lines.append(f'{k}: "{s}"')
>             else:
>                 out_lines.append(f"{k}: {s}")
>     return "\n".join(out_lines) + "\n"
> 
> 
> def classify_type(path: Path, binder: Optional[str]) -> str:
>     name = path.name
> 
>     # Templates
>     if binder == "templates":
>         return "template"
> 
>     # Archive
>     if binder == "archive":
>         # preserve "admin" if it's migration notes/logs
>         if "MIGRATION" in name.upper() or "PROMOTION" in name.upper():
>             return "admin"
>         return "legacy"
> 
>     # Vault root readme
>     if name.upper() == "README.MD" and path.parent.name == "FCFCU_CASE":
>         return "vault_root"
> 
>     # Master indexes
>     if "MASTER_CASE_INDEX" in name.upper() or "WAR_ROOM_OVERVIEW" in name.upper():
>         return "master_index"
> 
>     # Folder readmes
>     if name == "_README.md":
>         return "folder_index"
> 
>     # Section covers
>     if name.upper().endswith("SECTION_COVER.MD"):
>         return "section_cover"
> 
>     # Evidence maps/logs
>     if "EVIDENCE_LOG" in name.upper() or "EXHIBIT_MAP" in name.upper() or "RAW_EXHIBIT_MAP" in name.upper():
>         return "evidence_map"
> 
>     # Default court/war docs
>     return "court_doc" if binder in ("court", "war_room") else "scratch"
> 
> 
> def normalize_frontmatter(data: Dict[str, object]) -> Dict[str, object]:
>     # normalize common variants
>     key_map = {
>         "CaseID": "case_id",
>         "caseId": "case_id",
>         "Case_Id": "case_id",
>         "Type": "type",
>         "Binder": "binder",
>         "Tab": "tab",
>         "ID": "id",
>         "Tags": "tags",
>     }
>     normalized: Dict[str, object] = {}
>     for k, v in data.items():
>         nk = key_map.get(k, k)
>         normalized[nk] = v
>     return normalized
> 
> 
> def ensure_frontmatter(path: Path, text: str, apply_updated: bool = True) -> Tuple[str, bool, str]:
>     yaml_text, body = split_frontmatter(text)
>     changed = False
>     reasons: List[str] = []
> 
>     fm: Dict[str, object] = {}
>     if yaml_text is not None:
>         fm = normalize_frontmatter(parse_simple_yaml(yaml_text))
> 
>     binder = detect_binder(path) or fm.get("binder")
>     if binder and binder not in ("court", "war_room", "templates", "archive"):
>         # keep but don't trust it; overwrite later
>         pass
> 
>     # Set binder if derivable
>     derived_binder = detect_binder(path)
>     if derived_binder and fm.get("binder") != derived_binder:
>         fm["binder"] = derived_binder
>         changed = True
>         reasons.append(f"binder={derived_binder}")
> 
>     binder = fm.get("binder") if fm.get("binder") else derived_binder
> 
>     # Set case_id for court + war_room
>     if binder in ("court", "war_room"):
>         if fm.get("case_id") != CASE_ID:
>             fm["case_id"] = CASE_ID
>             changed = True
>             reasons.append("case_id")
> 
>     # Ensure type
>     desired_type = classify_type(path, binder if isinstance(binder, str) else None)
>     if fm.get("type") != desired_type:
>         fm["type"] = desired_type
>         changed = True
>         reasons.append(f"type={desired_type}")
> 
>     # Derive id/tab
>     doc_id, tab = derive_id_and_tab(path.name)
>     if doc_id and fm.get("id") != doc_id:
>         fm["id"] = doc_id
>         changed = True
>         reasons.append("id")
>     if tab and fm.get("tab") != tab:
>         fm["tab"] = tab
>         changed = True
>         reasons.append("tab")
> 
>     # Title
>     if not fm.get("title"):
>         fm["title"] = title_from_filename(path.name)
>         changed = True
>         reasons.append("title")
> 
>     # Validate type enum
>     if str(fm.get("type")) not in TYPE_ENUM:
>         # fallback
>         fm["type"] = "scratch"
>         changed = True
>         reasons.append("type_invalid->scratch")
> 
>     # Updated timestamp
>     if apply_updated and changed:
>         fm["updated"] = today_ymd()
> 
>     # If no YAML originally and binder indicates structured area, create YAML
>     needs_fm = binder in ("court", "war_room", "templates", "archive") or path.name == "_README.md"
>     if yaml_text is None and needs_fm:
>         changed = True
>         reasons.append("add_frontmatter")
> 
>     if not changed:
>         return text, False, "no_change"
> 
>     new_yaml = dump_simple_yaml(fm)
>     new_text = f"---\n{new_yaml}---\n\n{body.lstrip()}"
>     return new_text, True, ";".join(reasons)
> 
> 
> def build_folder_readme(folder: Path, binder: Optional[str]) -> str:
>     """
>     Creates deterministic folder _README.md content.
>     """
>     md_files = sorted([p for p in folder.iterdir() if p.is_file() and p.suffix.lower() == ".md" and p.name != "_README.md"])
>     subfolders = sorted([p for p in folder.iterdir() if p.is_dir() and not p.name.startswith(".")])
> 
>     title = f"Folder Index — {folder.name}"
> 
>     lines: List[str] = []
>     lines.append("---")
>     lines.append(f"title: {title}")
>     lines.append("type: folder_index")
>     if binder in ("court", "war_room"):
>         lines.append(f"case_id: {CASE_ID}")
>     if binder:
>         lines.append(f"binder: {binder}")
>     lines.append("---\n")
>     lines.append(f"# {title}\n")
> 
>     # Up links (best-effort)
>     # We keep this simple: just point to vault root; you can add more hand-tuned links later.
>     lines.append("## Up")
>     lines.append("- [[../../README|Vault Root]]" if "FCFCU_CASE" in folder.parts else "- [[README|Vault Root]]")
>     lines.append("")
> 
>     if subfolders:
>         lines.append("## Subfolders")
>         for sf in subfolders:
>             # Link to subfolder _README if exists/expected
>             lines.append(f"- **{sf.name}/**")
>         lines.append("")
> 
>     if md_files:
>         lines.append("## Notes")
>         for p in md_files:
>             display = p.stem.replace("_", " ")
>             lines.append(f"- [[{p.name}|{display}]]")
>         lines.append("")
> 
>     lines.append("## Notes")
>     lines.append("- Promotion status: (Court / War / Archive)")
>     lines.append("")
>     return "\n".join(lines)
> 
> 
> def should_index_folder(folder: Path) -> bool:
>     # Index folders that contain md files OR contain subfolders with md files
>     has_md = any(p.is_file() and p.suffix.lower() == ".md" for p in folder.iterdir())
>     if has_md:
>         return True
>     for sub in folder.iterdir():
>         if sub.is_dir() and not sub.name.startswith("."):
>             if any(p.is_file() and p.suffix.lower() == ".md" for p in sub.iterdir()):
>                 return True
>     return False
> 
> 
> def main():
>     ap = argparse.ArgumentParser(description="Fix front matter and rebuild folder indexes.")
>     ap.add_argument("--root", type=str, default=".", help="Root folder to scan (default: current dir).")
>     ap.add_argument("--write", action="store_true", help="Actually write changes. Without this, runs in dry-run mode.")
>     ap.add_argument("--no-folder-index", action="store_true", help="Do not generate/update _README.md folder indexes.")
>     ap.add_argument("--logdir", type=str, default=".", help="Where to write logs.")
>     args = ap.parse_args()
> 
>     root = Path(args.root).resolve()
>     logdir = Path(args.logdir).resolve()
>     logdir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
> 
>     log_md = logdir / "FRONTMATTER_FIX_LOG.md"
>     log_csv = logdir / "FRONTMATTER_FIX_LOG.csv"
> 
>     results: List[FixResult] = []
> 
>     # Pass 1: fix front matter
>     for path in root.rglob("*.md"):
>         if path.name in SKIP_FILENAMES:
>             continue
>         if any(part.startswith(".") for part in path.parts):
>             continue
> 
>         try:
>             text = path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")
>         except UnicodeDecodeError:
>             # fallback
>             text = path.read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="replace")
> 
>         new_text, changed, reason = ensure_frontmatter(path, text, apply_updated=True)
>         if changed:
>             results.append(FixResult(path=path, changed=True, reason=reason))
>             if args.write:
>                 path.write_text(new_text, encoding="utf-8")
>         else:
>             results.append(FixResult(path=path, changed=False, reason=reason))
> 
>     # Pass 2: folder indexes
>     folder_index_updates: List[FixResult] = []
>     if not args.no_folder_index:
>         for folder in sorted({p.parent for p in root.rglob("*.md")}):
>             if any(part.startswith(".") for part in folder.parts):
>                 continue
>             if not should_index_folder(folder):
>                 continue
> 
>             binder = detect_binder(folder)
>             readme_path = folder / "_README.md"
>             desired = build_folder_readme(folder, binder)
> 
>             existing = readme_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8") if readme_path.exists() else ""
>             if existing != desired:
>                 folder_index_updates.append(FixResult(path=readme_path, changed=True, reason="folder_index_update"))
>                 if args.write:
>                     readme_path.write_text(desired, encoding="utf-8")
>             else:
>                 folder_index_updates.append(FixResult(path=readme_path, changed=False, reason="no_change"))
> 
>     # Write logs
>     changed_count = sum(1 for r in results if r.changed) + sum(1 for r in folder_index_updates if r.changed)
>     now = dt.datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S")
> 
>     md_lines: List[str] = []
>     md_lines.append(f"# Front Matter + Index Fix Log\n")
>     md_lines.append(f"- Run at: {now}")
>     md_lines.append(f"- Root: `{root}`")
>     md_lines.append(f"- Mode: {'WRITE' if args.write else 'DRY-RUN'}")
>     md_lines.append(f"- Changes: {changed_count}\n")
> 
>     md_lines.append("## File Changes\n")
>     for r in results:
>         if r.changed:
>             md_lines.append(f"- ✅ `{r.path}` — {r.reason}")
>     for r in folder_index_updates:
>         if r.changed:
>             md_lines.append(f"- 📁 `{r.path}` — {r.reason}")
> 
>     md_lines.append("\n## Unchanged (sample)\n")
>     unchanged_sample = [r for r in results if not r.changed][:25]
>     for r in unchanged_sample:
>         md_lines.append(f"- ⏺ `{r.path}`")
> 
>     log_md.write_text("\n".join(md_lines) + "\n", encoding="utf-8")
> 
>     with log_csv.open("w", newline="", encoding="utf-8") as f:
>         w = csv.writer(f)
>         w.writerow(["path", "changed", "reason"])
>         for r in results + folder_index_updates:
>             w.writerow([str(r.path), "yes" if r.changed else "no", r.reason])
> 
>     print(f"Done. Changes={changed_count}. Log: {log_md.name}, {log_csv.name}")
> 
> 
> if __name__ == "__main__":
>     main()
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## How to run (no thinking required)
> 
> From `FCFCU_CASE` root:
> 
> **Dry run first:**
> ```powershell
> python .\fix_frontmatter_and_indexes.py --root . --logdir . 
> ```
> 
> **Then actually write:**
> ```powershell
> python .\fix_frontmatter_and_indexes.py --root . --logdir . --write
> ```
> 
> If you want it to skip folder `_README.md` generation:
> ```powershell
> python .\fix_frontmatter_and_indexes.py --root . --logdir . --write --no-folder-index
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## One fast decision before you run it
> Do you want `created:` to be auto-set?
> 
> Right now the script does **NOT** invent `created` (good for legal provenance). It only sets `updated` when it changes a file.
> 
> If you want `created`, the best rule is:
> - Use the date in the filename when present (like `2025-12-15_...`)
> - Else leave blank
> 
> If you answer “yes,” I’ll patch the script to extract filename dates into `created` without touching anything else.

### User

### Assistant
> You don’t need “help” — you need **a repeatable cover template + prefilled covers for each top-level binder section**, and optionally a generator script later. Let’s do the covers now.
> 
> ## Locked Section Cover Standard (for `*.00.000_SECTION_COVER.md`)
> 
> Every section cover should do four jobs:
> 1) Identify section (tab + code + case id)
> 2) Give the judge-ready “what this section proves”
> 3) Provide a quick map of subsections (links)
> 4) Call out “most-cited” docs in that section
> 
> ### Cover front matter (LOCKED)
> Use this on every section cover:
> 
> ```yaml
> title: "<TAB> — <SECTION NAME>"
> type: section_cover
> case_id: 49D03-2501-MF-002559
> binder: court
> tab: <TAB>
> id: <TABCODE>.00.000
> print: true
> visibility: internal_only
> updated: 2026-01-02
> tags:
>   - fcfcu
>   - court_binder
>   - section_cover
> ```
> 
> - `title` is human-facing.
> - `tab` is the binder letter (`A`, `B`, `C`, etc.).
> - `id` matches the filename prefix.
> - `print: true` forces these into any “print binder” workflow.
> - `updated` can be overwritten by your script later.
>

### User
> i found this does any of this something we might consider? Preparing a Court Bundle

> 

> Preparing a Court BundleA vital step when approaching trial

> 

> If ever the saying “time is money” were true, then it must be when you talk about lawyers. With the guideline hourly rate for a partner regularly exceeding £200 an hour, any steps which help to reduce the time spent on a case are worthwhile taking. 

> 

> As a case approaches a hearing in court, one method of reducing the time spent is by preparing a “court bundle”. Court bundles are usually required for any case that appears in court. The idea is that the judge will be able to pre-read all the relevant documents in the case. All the parties will also have all the evidence and copies of any precedents collected together in one place, making it easier to refer to information during the trial. In theory there is no reason why simply making copies of all the relevant documents in a case should be problematic, but it may not surprise you to learn that all kinds of problems happen in practice.

> 

> The main problem is the sheer amount of paperwork that needs to be dealt with. It is difficult to ensure that all the relevant documents in your own case are properly included, much less to check what the other side has included in the bundle. To give you an idea of the size of the task, a very small court bundle might run to several hundred pages. More often than not, a court bundle can be several thousand pages. If this were not bad enough, the bundle also has to be copied at least three times: one copy for you, one for the court and one for the other side. If you have counsel acting for the parties or more than one defendant, further copies would have to be prepared for them. The time involved just copying the documents is substantial, but even more time needs to be spent assembling, paginating (numbering the pages), checking and agreeing a bundle.

> 

> The responsibility for preparing the bundle usually falls to the party that made the application for a hearing. They are responsible for paginating it, which means that they will have to try their best to agree the contents with any other parties. 

> 

> Contents of a court bundle

> 

> A court bundle should contain copies of the following documents, in chronological order from the front of the bundle: 

> 

> (a)    Preliminary documents and any case management documents;

> (b)    Applications and orders;

> (c)    Statements and affidavits (which must be dated in the top right corner of the front page);

> (e)    Experts’ reports and other reports; and

> (f)    Any other documents, divided into further sections as appropriate.

> 

> In addition to these documents, some courts require up-to-date summaries of matters relevant to the hearing; statements of issues to be determined; position statements from each party, including a summary of orders sought; a chronology; skeleton arguments; and lists of essential reading.

> 

> Format of the bundle

> 

> Bundles are usually contained in one or more A4-size ring binders or lever arch files (each lever arch file being limited to about 350 pages).

> 

> All ring binders and lever arch files need to be clearly marked on the front and the spine with:

> 

> (a)    The title and number of the case;

> (b)    The court where the case has been listed;

> (c)    The hearing date and time;

> (d)    The name of the judge hearing the case (if known); and

> (e)    Where there is more than one ring binder or lever arch file, a distinguishing letter (A, B, C, etc.).

> 

> Timetable for preparing the bundle

> 

> Preparation of the bundle is often left until the last minute to potentially save on the cost of having to prepare it. This naturally can cause the person left to the task some difficulties, to put it mildly. Cases can have different deadlines for the bundle to be lodged, but as a general rule if less than a working week is left to prepare the documents, it is very likely that mistakes will be made. In the worst case, a bundle might not be lodged at all. If this happens, then the Court may decide that a hearing must be adjourned, and your firm will pay the costs incurred by your opponent.

> 

> As a legal secretary, you are probably highly organised and methodical. With these traits, you should approach the task of preparing a court bundle with confidence. Mastering this task will ensure that you are always in great demand in any litigation department. 

> 

> Example Content for a Simple Court Bundle

> 

> Description    

> 

> Statement of evidence      

> 

> Correspondence from claimant                         

> 

> Correspondence from defendant                      

> 

> Contract                                                          

> 

> Relevant case law summary                              

> 

> R v Stephens                                                    

> 

> UTCCR 1999                                                  

> 

> UCTA 1977                                                   

> 

> SOGA 1982                                                   

> 

> Terms & Condtions 1997                                 

> 

> Terms & Conditions 2005   

> 

> If you are interested in furthering your understanding of law and legal procedures, take a look at ILSPA's Legal Secretary courses. You can study their Legal Secretaries Diploma course covering various areas of law or take specific subjects through their Foundation and Advanced Level courses. These are suitable for aspiring and experienced Legal Secretaries as well as law graduates who want to get their foot in the door.  Related client or matter

> Type of document (contract, order, etc.)

> Version

> Subject

> Related Parties

> Over time, this creates long, unwieldy files names such as:

> 

> XYZCo-IPMatter-Patent-Fililng-USPTO-V3.docx

> The problem with this approach is that the law firm is trying to cram a lot of metadata into the name of the file.  Doing so is using the wrong tool for the job.

> 

> A proper DMS includes functionality for tagging and profiling documents as needed, and allows you to code things like Document Type, Status, Matter and so forth in the DMS. Correspondence

> 

> (subsections for letters/emails/faxes, and one for fee agreements)

> 

> 2. Pleadings

> 

> (subsections for different courts)

> 

> 3. Drafts

> 

> 4. Discovery

> 

> (subsections for propounded, received, drafts)

> 

> 5. Documents

> 

> (subsections for documents received from client, documents to disclose, and documents provided by client, as well as received from other parties)

> 

> 6. Experts

> 

> (subfolders for each expert, plus another one for opposing expert reports)

> 

> 7. Depositions

> 

> (subfolders for each deponent)

> 

> 8. Research

> 

> 9. Misc.

> 

> Others have billing. That's a separate program in our system.

>

> u/JuDGe3690 avatar

> JuDGe3690

> •

> 1y ago

> One fundamental thing that I didn't see here is to use a consistent file naming convention, preferably ISO-compliant. I prefer YYYY-MM-DD to start, then include client name and document description (to be readable when searching as well as navigating folders). The nice thing with the Year-Month-Day format is it automatically sorts chronologically when set alphabetical, either Old-to-New in ascending order, or New-to-Old in descending order.

>

> Our firm has Worldox and idk if it comes like that or if our IT has created them and we have like five million possible categories that get confusing when you have multiple people and teams using it but here are the main ones that are pretty standard across the firm:

> 

> Correspondence

> 

> Emails

> 

> Client Correspondence

> 

> Client Documents

> 

> Documents produced by other parties

> 

> Pleadings

> 

> Discovery

> 

> Drafts

> 

> Motions

> 

> Experts

> 

> Records (subpoenaed)

> 

> Summaries

> 

> Photos

> 

> Depositions

> 

> I do insurance defense too so we have a folder for Carrier Emails and Approvals, so when we need to create a paper trail for things like authority to offer X in settlement or retain certain experts.

> 

> I will say if you're planning on going to trial often you will need sub categories for that. Whenever we've gone to trial the formal Trial folder just becomes the catch all for trial documents, daily transcripts, motion work, pocket briefs, etc. and it's a nightmare.

### Assistant
> Good find. Yes—what you pasted **confirms you’re on the right track**, and it also helps us lock this down cleanly instead of over-engineering it.
> 
> Let’s do this in **two clean passes**:
> 
> ---
> 
> ## PASS 1 — LOCK THE FRONT MATTER (NO CODE YET)
> 
> This is the **canonical front matter schema** for *everything* in this case ecosystem.  
> It works for:
> 
> - Court binder exports  
> - War Room (internal)  
> - Obsidian navigation  
> - Index generation  
> - Later audit / undue-burden logs  
> 
> ### ✅ **NON-NEGOTIABLE RULES**
> - Front matter **always present**
> - Same schema everywhere
> - No metadata in filenames except **ordering prefix**
> - Content decides visibility, not filename
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 🔒 CANONICAL FRONT MATTER (v1 — LOCK THIS)
> 
> ```yaml
> ---
> id: <auto or filename>
> title: "<Human-readable title>"
> section: "<A | B | C | D | E | F | G | H | I | J>"
> tab: "<Anchor | Overview | Jurisdiction | Motions | Evidence | Timeline | Relief | Orders | Record | Appendix>"
> role: "<court | judge | opposing | internal | archive>"
> status: "<active | supporting | background | draft | archived>"
> visibility: "<print | sleeve | internal-only>"
> document_type: "<motion | order | exhibit | affidavit | declaration | timeline | index | strategy | note>"
> source: "<court record | defendant | plaintiff | sheriff | third-party>"
> related_case: "49D03-2501-MF-002559"
> date: YYYY-MM-DD
> hearing_relevance: "<core | supporting | none>"
> exhibit_id: "<A | B | C | ... | 0101 | 0102 | none>"
> binder_volume: "<A | B | C | none>"
> war_room: true|false
> notes: "<optional short note>"
> ---
> ```
> 
> This is **deliberate**. Here’s why.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## WHY THIS WORKS (AND WHY WE DON’T ADD MORE)
> 
> ### 1. **Section + Tab = physical binder mapping**
> - `section` = LETTER ON TAB  
> - `tab` = human meaning  
> You can hand this to a judge or reconstruct it at FedEx half asleep.
> 
> ### 2. **role + visibility prevent mistakes**
> This directly answers your fear of:
> > “don’t accidentally let nobody see this”
> 
> - `role: internal`
> - `visibility: internal-only`
> 
> Your red binder ≠ printable by accident.
> 
> ### 3. **document_type enables automation**
> Your future scripts will:
> - auto-build exhibit lists  
> - auto-build indices  
> - auto-flag missing affidavits  
> without guessing.
> 
> ### 4. **exhibit_id is optional and late-binding**
> This solves your earlier concern about inserting later:
> 
> - Drafts → `exhibit_id: none`
> - Locked → `exhibit_id: 0104`
> - Insert later → `0104.1`, `0104.2`
> 
> No renaming chaos.
> 
> ### 5. **war_room flag = parallel universe**
> This is the elegant part.
> 
> Same structure.  
> Same numbering.  
> Different intent.
> 
> ```yaml
> war_room: true
> ```
> 
> Now you can:
> - mirror folders
> - selectively export
> - prove restraint later if needed
> 
> ---
> 
> ## WHAT WE ARE **NOT** DOING (ON PURPOSE)
> 
> ❌ No ISO timestamps in filenames  
> ❌ No client/matter stuffed into filenames  
> ❌ No DMS-style metadata abuse  
> ❌ No UK-style “bundle B(iii)(f)” nonsense  
> 
> Why? Because **you are pro se, under time pressure, and this must survive printing at FedEx**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## EXAMPLE — REAL FILE (COURT-READY)
> 
> ```yaml
> ---
> id: C-0110-001
> title: "Sheriff Return – March 5, 2025"
> section: C
> tab: Jurisdiction
> role: court
> status: active
> visibility: print
> document_type: exhibit
> source: sheriff
> related_case: "49D03-2501-MF-002559"
> date: 2025-03-05
> hearing_relevance: core
> exhibit_id: A
> binder_volume: A
> war_room: false
> notes: "No mailing indicated as required by TR 4.1(B)"
> ---
> ```
> 
> This is **judge-brain compatible**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## PASS 2 (NEXT) — WHAT I WILL DO AFTER YOU CONFIRM
> 
> Once you say **“Lock it”**, I will:
> 
> 1. Give you a **Python script** that:
>    - scans all `.md`
>    - inserts missing front matter
>    - normalizes keys
>    - flags conflicts
>    - logs every change (for undue-burden defense)
> 
> 2. Give you an **index builder** that:
>    - respects `visibility`
>    - outputs:
>      - Court Binder Index
>      - Judge Copy Index
>      - War Room Index
> 
> 3. Give you a **FedEx-safe export plan**
>    - one click → PDF per tab
>    - correct order
>    - no leaks
> 
> ---
> 
> ## FINAL QUESTION (ONLY ONE)
> 
> Do you want:
> - **`id` auto-generated** (safer, faster), or  
> - **`id` derived from filename** (human readable)?
> 
> Answer that, or say **“Lock it as-is”**, and we move straight into the script.

### User
> where do the original complaints and case docs go, whih tab

### Assistant
> Short, direct answer — **they go in TAB H**, with one important refinement.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 🔑 RULE OF THUMB (LOCK THIS IN)
> 
> **If it was filed by the plaintiff or issued by the court and is part of the official case record → TAB H (Court Record / Docket Evidence).**
> 
> You do **not** argue from these documents.  
> You **anchor** your arguments to them.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## EXACT PLACEMENT
> 
> ### ✅ **TAB H — COURT RECORD & DOCKET EXCERPTS**
> This is where the **original complaint and core case documents live**.
> 
> **Include here (printed, paginated, sleeved):**
> - Original **Complaint**
> - Amended Complaint(s) (if any)
> - Summons(es)
> - Praecipe(s)
> - Default Judgment Motion(s)
> - Orders entered
> - Petition for Writ of Assistance
> - Writ of Assistance
> - Sheriff’s returns
> - Docket printout / Odyssey entries (relevant pages only)
> 
> These are **Exhibits**, even if they were filed by the other side.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## WHY NOT TAB A, B, OR C?
> 
> - **TAB A (Anchor / Overview)**  
>   ❌ No raw filings — summaries only
> 
> - **TAB B (Legal Basis)**  
>   ❌ Law + analysis, not evidence
> 
> - **TAB C (Motions)**  
>   ❌ Your filings only
> 
> Judges expect **the complaint and court-generated documents to be together** in a record section, not scattered.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## HOW TO STRUCTURE TAB H (IMPORTANT)
> 
> Inside **TAB H**, subdivide like this:
> 
> ```
> H7_COURT_RECORD/
> ├── H7.01_COMPLAINT_AND_PLEADINGS/
> │   ├── H7.01.001_Original_Complaint.pdf
> │   ├── H7.01.002_Amended_Complaint.pdf
> │
> ├── H7.02_SERVICE_AND_SUMMONS/
> │   ├── H7.02.001_Summons_1.pdf
> │   ├── H7.02.002_Sheriff_Return_03-05-2025.pdf
> │
> ├── H7.03_MOTIONS_AND_ORDERS/
> │   ├── H7.03.001_Motion_Default_Judgment.pdf
> │   ├── H7.03.002_Order_Denying_Default.pdf
> │
> ├── H7.04_WRIT_AND_ENFORCEMENT/
> │   ├── H7.04.001_Petition_for_Writ.pdf
> │   ├── H7.04.002_Writ_of_Assistance.pdf
> │
> └── H7.05_DOCKET/
>     ├── H7.05.001_Docket_Snapshot.pdf
> ```
> 
> This mirrors **how judges mentally model a case file**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## CROSS-REFERENCE RULE (CRITICAL)
> 
> - **TAB H = “What exists in the record”**
> - **TAB B / C / D / E = “Why that record is defective or unlawful”**
> 
> So in your motions you say things like:
> 
> > “As shown in **Exhibit H7.02.001**, service was not completed in accordance with Trial Rule 4.1(B)….”
> 
> That’s clean. That’s professional. That’s persuasive.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## WAR ROOM MIRROR (FOR YOUR SANITY)
> 
> In the **WAR ROOM**, the mirror is:
> 
> - **WH — Evidence Vault (Official Record)**
> 
> Same docs, same numbering, but you can annotate, highlight, and strategize freely there.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## FINAL LOCK-IN STATEMENT
> 
> > **Original complaint and all plaintiff/court filings belong in TAB H — Court Record & Docket Excerpts.**
> 
> If you want, next I can:
> - sanity-check your current TAB H against this rule, or  
> - give you the **front matter preset specifically for court-record documents** so the script handles them correctly.
